template for the Missoula National Bank's articles of incorporation), a copy of
the 1873 Articles of Incorporation for the Missoula National Bank, and a 1913
amendment to the First Nationa Montana Bank of Missoula's Articles of
Incorporation. These materials document the early organization of one of
western Montana's first corporate ventures.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains financial records from the First National
Bank, primarily bound ledgers. Materials include general operating ledgers,
individual account records, daily balance logs, regulatory reports of assets
and liabilities, cash and credit transaction documents, and client signature
books. Federal records include reports to and notices from the U.S. Treasury
Department. Materials in this series present significant documentation of
Missoula's early economic history, the town's foundational business
relationships, the ebb and flow of western Montana economic development from
the late nineteenth century through the early twentieth century, the impacts of
national procedural/regulatory changes upon rural banks, and daily operations
at the Missoula institution.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains three newspaper scrapbooks detailing
developments within the First National Bank from 1903-1939, samples of internal
forms, and two examples of Bank promotional materials. The items in this series
provide broad insights into First National Bank operations and public
relations.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains financial records from the Missoula Trust and
Savings Bank. The exact relationship between Missoula Trust and Savings Bank
and the First National Bank is not established by collection materials.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains general correspondence, financial records,
legal documents, clippings, and miscellany. Included are personal letters,
1893-1972; records of household finances, 1946-1957; income tax forms,
1936-1972; certificates, 1887-1935; memorial records, 1966-1972; and newspaper
clippings. Two letters to the MacIvors dated Jan. 21, 1922 and February 8,
1922, give details of an automobile trip from Butte, Montana to Portland,
Oregon. Two folders of previously unincorporated photographs were added into
the collection in 2006.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes early personal correspondence to Nell and her
sister, Eliza, from both their brother, Asa Crockett, and father, Daniel W.
Crockett. There is later personal correspondence between Nell and Donald
MacIvor. A few letters concern Mr. MacIvor's attempt to get a temporary release
from the railroad in 1918 in order to gain an officer's commission in the army.
Instead of gaining an officer's commission, Mr. MacIvor became chairman of the
United War Campaign which raised funds for the war effort. Folder 2 contains a
practice exam given to immigrants who desired United States citizenship. This
folder also includes two letters describing an automobile trip from Butte,
Montana to Portland, Oregon in 1921. Folder 3 contains a description of a trip
to Jerusalem from Beirut in 1951 and other correspondence to the MacIvors
describing life in the Middle East in the 1950s. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series contains records of the MacIvor's household finances
while living in Missoula from 1944-1957. Examples of expenses included furnace
oil, electric lights, and rent. A primary source of income was Mr. MacIvor's
railroad pension. The second folder contains the MacIvor's state and federal
income tax forms from 1936-1972.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series contains Nell's birth certificate, high school
diploma, and a Diploma of Progress from the Methodist Episcopal Church. It also
includes Donald's Military Registration Certificate, Notice of Military
Classification, and membership cards for the Liberty Loan Committee.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series primarily includes newspaper clippings about Judge Asa
James Crockett, who was related to Nell.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series contains a memorial book for Judge Asa James Crockett
who died in 1966. This book includes a brief family history. There is also a
memorial for Nell MacIvor, who died in 1972. There is an address book and two
valentines. The valentines were sent to Nell from Donald dated circa 1907.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Photographs include formal portraits and snapshots of people and
scenes, including images from the Bearmouth, Montana, and Hopewell, Nova
Scotia. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520" id="a3">
<p>This is a collection of newsletters, handbooks, and pamphlets. It includes copies of the
annual MIEA handbook, which was prepared jointly by the University of Montana School of Journalism and
MIEA and served as a directory of publications and publication advisors at Montana
high schools. The collection also contains copies of the MIEA newsletter, <title type="italics">The
Editor</title>, from 1957 to 1975 which was published several times during the school year.
The MIEA advisor, often a faculty member of the Journalism School, served as editor
of the newsletter. </p>

</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection is divided into four series.</p>
<p>Series I: Correspondence (1919-1985) The bulk of the correspondence is
letters to Clarice Cushman from her husband, William Cushman, when he was away
from home in the U.S. Navy during WWII, in Liberia for four years, in the Warm
Springs mental health facility in Montana, and in the Veterans Hospital in
Sheridan, Wyoming. The letters chronicle the family’s daily lives, the
centrality of religious beliefs, marital discord, and four decades of Clarice
Cushman’s attempts to find medical and education assistance for their son,
Roger Cushman, who had severe disabilities. The correspondence also includes
letters from relatives, friends and institutions, letters received by William
Cushman, and letters received by Roger Cushman.</p>
<p>Series II: Diaries and Scrapbooks (1920-1971) includes Clarice
Cushman’s diaries, that begin a few years before her marriage to William
Cushman in 1935 and end during WWII. Her sometimes daily brief entries reveal
her daily activities, social contacts, and later interactions with her husband.
The more sporadic entries in William Cushman’s diaries describe his work and
include one lengthier examination of his feelings about his marriage and his
wife while they are apart. Clarice Cushman’s scrapbook (1920-1925) contains
photos and memorabilia of her school years beginning in high school and ending
when she is awarded a teaching certificate. The other two scrapbooks of local
music and school events may have been done as an exercise with the Cushman’s
son, Roger.</p>
<p>Series III: Financial Records (1928-1968) consists of a few scattered
bank records and some daily and weekly income and expenditure lists.</p>
<p>Series IV: Miscellaneous (1918-1974) consists of memorabilia from high
school, weddings, and births as well as various types of personal
identification, a genealogy, church programs, and religious tracts. The few
identified photos are of the Cushmans around the late 1930s.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The collection consists of Garlington's papers from the 1972 Montana
Constitutional Convention. It contains a daily journal kept by Garlington, his
campaign expenditures and some speeches, legal material dealing with the
election recount, newspaper articles on the Convention and Missoula delegates,
a copy of the Montana revised codes, and correspondence between Garlington and
others. Publications in the collection concern the drafting of state
constitutions. A voter's guide has short biographies of all Convention
delegates.</p>
<p>From the Convention itself are draft proposals and letters of
transmittal from committees on the executive, education, natural resource and
agriculture, judicial committees, and legislative committees. Also contained in
the collection are various member proposals, educational material sponsored by
the Society of American Foresters and Office of Public Instruction, a
resolution calling for submittal of the proposed constitution to the voters,
and highlights of the proposed constitution.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains the journal that Garlington kept throughout
the Convention, and consists mainly of his notes on each day's events. It
includes many copies of minutes, proposals, and other inserts.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains Garlington's correspondence related to the
Convention. It contains letters congratulating him on his election, requests to
focus on particular issues, and other matters. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains records of Garlington's election, including
campaign materials, speeches, the recount challenge, and the financial records
from the campaign. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains materials from the Convention, including the
activities of committees. It also contains Garlington's appointment certificate
and materials about the Convention delegates. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains clippings from Montana newspapers about the
Convention and its activities.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection is an original charter from the National Farmers'
Alliance authorizing the formation of the Carlton Farmers’ Alliance No.6, in
Stevensville, Montana, on December 17, 1890. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The Boone and Crockett Club Records have been divided into six Series,
most of which have been further subdivided. The largest series in this
collection is Series I: Administration, which contains early administrative
correspondence and Executive Committee minutes, almost an entire run of the
minutes of the Club’s annual meetings which began in 1893, and an almost
complete run of Officer, Committee, and Membership booklets which were produced
by the Club each year. </p>
<p>This collection also includes materials documenting the Club’s
involvement in the big game conservation history of North America including
general correspondence, Game Preservation Committee and Conservation Committee
meeting minutes and correspondence, and materials documenting the Boone and
Crockett Club’s Conservation Grants Program. The collection also contains
materials that relate to the Boone and Crockett Club’s big game records keeping
activities. These materials include documents pertaining to North American Big
Game Records Competitions and Awards Programs, Records of North American Big
Game Committee meeting minutes and correspondence files, the materials produced
by the administrative staff of the Club’s Big Game Records Division, and
materials related to the National Collection of Heads and Horns. Additionally,
the records include documents related to the Boone and Crockett Club’s
publications including administrative correspondence, planning materials and
drafts of the Club’s records books, and drafts and correspondence related to
the Club’s
<title>Fair Chase</title> magazine.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains materials related to the administrative
division of the Boone and Crockett Club, including general correspondence,
officer and committee reports, meeting minutes, and materials related to the
Club’s annual and other member meetings. The Series has been divided into
twelve subseries, most of which have been subdivided further into
sub-subseries. </p>
<p>Materials were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect
the historic and current organization of the Club’s administration. Series are
arranged alphabetically. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This subseries contains drafts of the Club’s constitution,
by-laws, and incorporation. It documents the evolution of the Club’s by-laws as
it contains correspondence regarding amendments and proposed changes dating
from 1922 through 1993. Additionally, the series contains drafts and proposed
amendments of the Club’s constitution and documents the evolution of the Club’s
statement of purpose.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This subseries contains a run of general correspondence that
documents the grassroots development of the Club. Although correspondence
before 1891 that would document the founding of the Club is missing from the
collection, early incoming and outgoing correspondence by founding Club members
George Bird Grinnell and Theodore Roosevelt is included in this subseries.
Additionally, the subseries contains materials that document the Club’s
organizational development. Although this early correspondence does document
the Club’s involvement in conservation and publications, specific
correspondence regarding these subjects and big game records can be found in
Series’ II, III, and IV.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This subseries contains annual reports, ledgers, financial
statements and correspondence, budget and tax materials, and materials related
to bequests, gifts and legacies left to the Club by members in their wills.
Materials such as cancelled checks, invoices and receipts dated post-1950 have
been removed from the collection.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This subseries is divided into 3 sub-subseries and contains
materials generated by the Executive Officers of the Club as well as other
administrative committees. Materials include meeting minutes, correspondence,
and reports.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-series contains correspondence and reports created by
individual members in their capacity as Executive Officers. The files arrived
at the archives in folders which appear to contain materials from a single
member and be limited to that member’s work as an officer of the Club. This
sub-subseries was created to reflect that organization and original order
within folders was maintained. Folders are arranged alphabetically by a
member’s last name and present an almost complete picture of the role of
Executive officers in the Boone and Crockett Club.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The executive committee of the Boone and Crockett Club was
responsible for the general administration of the Club in conjunction with
executive officers. This sub-subseries contains an almost entire run of
executive committee meeting minutes dating from the Club’s earliest official
meeting in 1888 through 2000. The Club would eventually transition from an
executive committee to a board of directors, as is the current administrative
organization.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains administrative committee materials
not created by the executive committee. Materials include correspondence,
minutes, and reports. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Annual membership gatherings have been a cornerstone of the Club
since its inception. The founding members believed that meetings and
discussions between members kept the membership active and engaged in
conservation issues. This subseries has been divided into three sub-subseries.
</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains the minutes of over 100 years of
the Club’s annual meetings, which document membership involvement in the
conservation, big game records keeping, and foundation goals of the Club. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries includes planning materials,
correspondence, and committee materials related to the Club’s Centennial
Celebration which took place in 1988 in Dallas, Texas.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>In addition to the Club’s annual meetings, membership was
often invited to attend casual meetings throughout the year. In the early years
of the Club these meetings included presentations and slideshows of hunts by
individual members. Later, the Club moved to have membership officially meet
quarterly. This sub-subseries contains meeting minutes, correspondence, and
planning materials for these events.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains minutes, correspondence, member mailers,
membership election ballots, and Membership Committee materials. The subseries
includes almost an entire run of Club yearbooks which document Club membership,
officers, and committee involvement dating from 1906 to the present. The
subseries also documents the process for obtaining regular membership as it
includes membership endorsements and sponsorships.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, appraisals, and
inventories pertaining to the Club library that contains materials owned by the
Roosevelt family and gifted to the Club by other members.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries includes correspondence, committee materials and
minutes, inventories and materials and plans related to the purchase and
remodel of the Old Milwaukee Railroad Depot (the Club’s current headquarters in
Missoula, Montana). Of possible interest in this series are materials
documenting the ownership of Guns gifted to the Club by the Roosevelt family
and currently stored at the Sagamore Hill National Historic Site in Oyster Bay,
New York. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains committee minutes, correspondence, and
materials related to various unpublished histories written about the Club. This
subseries also contains materials related to the Oral History project started
by the Club to document its history through interviews with longtime members.
</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries includes drafts and copies of dedications,
eulogies, speeches, and other statements given by Club members.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This subseries is divided into two sub-subseries and documents
the administration of Club offices. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Sub sub-series 1 includes office policies, stationary, general
inquiries and other materials related to office administration. Of particular
interest in this sub-subseries are folders that document the move of the Club’s
headquarters from Pittsburgh to Virginia and from Virginia to Montana.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Beginning in 1981, the Club employed an administrative
director and the position changed title to executive director by 1985. This
sub-subseries contains correspondence generated by office administrators and
executive directors of the Club. Correspondence from professional staff
employed in the big game records and publications divisions of the Club is
filed in series III and IV respectively. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains articles, clippings, correspondence, and
additional materials.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>Since its inception, the Boone and Crockett Club has been actively
involved in conservation issues. This series documents the Club’s conservation
activity from its early efforts to preserve game habitat through present-day
efforts to fund educational activities. This series has been divided into five
subseries and includes committee meeting minutes, correspondence, conservation
grant requests and progress reports, and materials related to collaborative
efforts and campaigns. Included in this series are materials related to the
Club’s concept of Fair Chase. </p>
<p>Materials were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect
the historic and current organization of the Club’s conservation efforts.
Series are arranged alphabetically. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries documents the conservation efforts of the Boone
and Crockett Club that took place before the Conservation Committee was formed
in 1947. Materials include correspondence, meeting minutes and reports from the
Game Preservation Committee (of which George Bird Grinnell was chair) which
documents the Club’s involvement in the designation of Glacier and Mt. McKinley
National Parks. Also included are materials related to the Club’s conservation
positions and policies. Absent are documents related to the Club’s involvement
in conservation activities before 1904. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The Conservation Committee of the Boone and Crockett Club was
formed in 1947 to address the Club’s conservation policies and actions. Various
subcommittees were organized throughout the existence of the Conservation
Committee and by 1994 the committee would include three standing
sub-committees; one that oversaw the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch, one
that worked with the Club’s university professorship programs, and one that
oversaw grants-in-aid. By 1998, the Club had reorganized its committees and
created the Hunter and Conservation Ethics Committee and the Position Papers
Committee. The Ranch subcommittee, Professorship subcommittee and Grants-in-aid
subcommittee became full committees. This subseries has been divided into four
sub-subseries reflecting the work of the Conservation Committee. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Of particular interest within this sub-subseries is an almost
complete run of the Conservation Committee’s correspondence and reports from
1947 through 1991. This sub-subseries also contains materials documenting the
Club’s efforts to assist in the support of game refuges including their
assistance in the creation of the Key Deer Refuge in Florida. Additionally,
this sub-subseries contains a print designed by cartoonist and Club member Jay
Norwood “Ding” Darling after the designation of the Key Deer Refuge. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains grant proposals, project reports,
and grants-in-aid subcommittee meeting minutes. The sub-subseries documents the
research the Club supported from 1959 through 2001, including early Isle Royale
Wolf Research and Predator-Prey studies. Absent are materials documenting Club
grant-in-aid support for projects between the late 1940s and 1959.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This Sub-subseries contains applications, correspondence,
proposals and progress reports related to the Club’s Conservation Grants
Program. The materials also include correspondence, and review materials
created by the Grants-in-Aid subcommittee, a subcommittee of the Conservation
Committee. These materials arrived at the archives in 2011, after other
Conservation Grant files had been organized. The 2011 addition arrived arranged
chronologically by the Boone and Crockett Club. This order was maintained, as
was original order within folders. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries documents the development of Boone and
Crockett conservation workshops of the 1970s. This sub-subseries demonstrates
the Club’s national and international involvement and collaboration in
conservation. Of particular interest in this sub-subseries are materials
documenting the Club’s involvement in the National Forest System Centennial
Celebration and the National Wildlife Conservation Partners Summit that was
hosted by the Club.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains articles, clippings,
correspondence, and additional materials.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The idea of fair chase was first proposed by Theodore Roosevelt
and was present in the original Club constitution. It prohibited “killing bear
or cougar in traps, crusting moose, elk or deer in deep snow, jacking, or
killing them from a boat.” This subseries documents the evolution of the Club’s
Fair Chase policy from the early 1960s through the late 1990s. </p>
<p>This subseries also includes materials related to the Club’s
positions on a wide variety of topics from gun control, private property
rights, and animal rights to the reintroduction of the wolf in Yellowstone
National Park. Researchers will find materials documenting the development of
these positions as well as responses from Club members to the Club’s position
papers. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, endorsements, and
additional materials related to conservation awards given to Club members as
well as conservation awards given by the Club. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, promotional packets,
catalogs and mailers related to the Club’s conservation and fundraising
campaigns. Included here are materials related to the Club’s conservation stamp
print fundraising effort as well as the Blazing New Trails for Conservation
campaign.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This series documents the Club’s big game records activities
including the evolution of the management of the Big Game Records program as
well as materials related to Official Measurers, the Sagamore Hill Medal
Program, and the National Collection of Heads and Horns. This series has been
divided into five subseries and includes committee meeting minutes,
correspondence, Awards Program planning materials, menus, invitations and
trophy certificates, as well as correspondence and inventories related to the
National Collection of Heads and Horns. </p>
<p>Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no
discernable original order and were grouped and interfiled by the processor to
reflect historic and current organization of the Club’s big game records
keeping activities and management. Series are arranged alphabetically and
original order within folders was maintained. </p>
<p>Note: Trophy records and related photographs are maintained at the
Boone and Crockett Club headquarters in their Big Game Records Department.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries has been divided into three subseries and
documents the administration of the club’s big game records program.
Established in 1935, the Records of North American Big Game Committee
supervised the Big Game Competitions until the Club began collaborating on Big
Game Records with the National Rifle Association in 1973. At that time, the
administrative duties fell to the North American Big Game Awards Program, which
was housed in the Hunting Activities Department of the National Rifle
Association. Currently, Big Game Records are administered in collaboration with
the North American Big Game Committee and professional staff. </p>
<p>This subseries is divided into three sub-subseries which reflect
the evolution of the management of Big Game Records at the Boone and Crockett
Club. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains materials related to committee
involvement in Big Game Records keeping. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Sub-sub-subseries 1 includes materials produced by the
Records of North American big Game Committee. In the years from 1935 through
1973, the Committee managed and oversaw the Club’s big game records-keeping
efforts including the North American Big Game Awards Programs. Of particular
interest are correspondence to and from Grancel and Betty Fitz that documents
changes in the trophy scoring system. Additionally, this sub-sub-subseries
contains meeting minutes, correspondence, trophy score sheets and materials
related to scoring from 1939 through 1993. Absent are correspondence or meeting
minutes created by the Committee before 1944. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Sub-sub-subseries 2 includes materials created by the
Friends of North American Big Game Committee, a group that financially
supported the North American Big Game Committee through subscriptions from the
early 1950s through the early 1960s. Materials include correspondence, big game
census figures and subscription information. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Sub-sub-subseries 3 includes materials produced by ad hoc
committees related to Big Game Records. This sub-sub-subseries contains
correspondence, memorandum and score chart revisions. Of particular interest
are materials related to the development of the trophy scoring system by Samuel
B. Webb that took place in the late 1940s and early 1950s. It is this scoring
system that became the standard for big game trophy measurement after its
development and is still in use today.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The North American Big Game Awards Program was a joint venture
between the Boone and Crockett Club and the National Rifle Association to
administer the Club’s big game records keeping responsibilities and Awards
Programs. The North American Big Game Awards Program was in existence from 1973
through late 1980, when the partnership dissolved.</p>
<p> This Sub-subseries contains meeting minutes, correspondence,
trophy score sheets and materials related to scoring. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This Sub-subseries contains materials created by the
professional staff tasked with administering the Club’s Big Game Records
program first in conjunction with the National Rifle Association, and since
1980, with the Boone and Crockett Club’s Records of North American Big Game
Committee. Materials include correspondence with trophy owners as well as the
Records of North American Big Game Committee and the National Rifle
Association. </p>
<p>The materials in this Sub-subseries document the evolution of
the Club’s Big Game Records program from being administered solely by members
acting as volunteers to that of a partnership between paid staff and Club
Committee members. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This Boone and Crockett Club has held North American Big Game
Awards Programs since 1947. This Subseries contains materials from the first
North American Big Game Competition in 1947 through the 24th North American Big
Game Awards held in 2001. Materials include correspondence, awardees lists,
banquet invitations, planning and promotional materials, programs, and judging
materials. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Created in 1948, the Sagamore Hill Medal is given by the
Roosevelt family in honor of Theodore Roosevelt, Theodore Roosevelt, Jr., and
Kermit Roosevelt. It is awarded by the Big Game Final Awards Judges panel to an
outstanding trophy of distinction. Only one is given at any Big Game Awards
Program and one need not be awarded at each Program. This Subseries contains
certificates, correspondence and committee materials related to the Medal
Program.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>Official Measurers of the Boone and Crockett Club are volunteers
who are certified by the Club to measure big game trophies. All trophies
entered into a Records of North American Big Game Awards Program must be
measured by a Boone and Crockett Club Official Measurer. Official Measurers
have been utilized by the Boone and Crockett Club since the late 1940s. </p>
<p>This subseries contains correspondence between Official
Measurers and Big Game Records professional staff, and the Records of North
American Big Game Committee, and Official Measurer manual drafts. Of particular
interest are materials related to Official Measurer training workshops
developed by William H. Nesbitt, Administrative Director of the North American
Big Game Records Program. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The National Collection of Heads and Horns was established by
Club member William T. Hornaday and was displayed at the Bronx Zoo in New York
City beginning in 1922. The collection is currently held at the Buffalo Bill
Historical Center in Cody, Wyoming and is maintained by the Boone and Crockett
Club. </p>
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, committee reports,
inventories dating from 1906 through 1978, promotional materials, and trophy
prints. Of particular interest are the research notes of Lowell E. Baier which
provide a history of the National Collection of Heads and Horns. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This series documents the Boone and Crockett Club’s outreach,
publicity, promotions and publications. The series has been divided into four
subseries and includes correspondence, drafts of publications, materials
related to the Club’s Fair Chase magazine, the Club’s newsletter, the Club’s
Associate’s Program and licensing and copyright materials. </p>
<p>Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no
discernable original order to the files and were grouped and interfiled by the
processor to reflect historic and current organization of the Club’s
communications division. Series are arranged alphabetically. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>An Editorial Committee was formed at the first official meeting
of the Boone and Crockett Club in 1888, and the Club has published materials
related to big game, conservation, and hunting since 1893. This subseries
contains five sub-subseries which include materials related to the Club’s
published materials.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains materials created by both the
Editorial and Historical committees of the Boone and Crockett Club from the
late 1950s through the late 1980s, as well as materials created by paid
professional staff. Items include committee meeting minutes, correspondence,
book orders, inventories, and publication lists. Absent are materials related
to items published before 1910.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries is divided into two sub-sub-subseries and
contains materials related to the books published by the Boone and Crockett
Club.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The first edition of <emph>Records of North American Big
Game</emph> was published by the Club in 1932 in conjunction with the National
Collection of Heads and Horns. After 1952 Records books were published every
six to seven years. In 1993 it was determined that Records books would be
published every six years. </p>
<p>This sub-sub-subseries contains materials from the first
edition of <emph>Records of North American Big Game</emph>, published in 1932,
through the tenth edition published in 1993. Materials include correspondence,
drafts, signatures, proofs, and big game score charts. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>In addition to the <emph>Records of North American Big
Game</emph> books, the Boone and Crockett has published editions on wild sheep,
record whitetail and mule deer as well as record elk. The club has also
published books on hunting and conservation. This sub-sub-subseries contains
correspondence, drafts, proofs, mailers and reviews related to these
publications.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>Established in 1994, <emph>Fair Chase</emph> magazine is
distributed quarterly to Associate Members of the Club. This sub-subseries
contains article drafts for the magazine and correspondence. Absent is a
published run of the magazine.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains materials related to the Club’s
newsletter that is distributed quarterly to regular members of the Club.
Materials include correspondence and a run of the newsletters from 1985 through
2001.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This sub-subseries contains correspondence, drafts, and
memoranda of miscellaneous volumes published by the Club.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The Boone and Crockett Club Associates Program was originally
proposed by William I. Spencer in 1984. The program was developed to involve
individuals who were interested in furthering the causes and work of the Club,
but didn’t fit the requirements for regular membership as outlined in the
Club’s constitution. An Associates Newsletter (which later developed into
<emph>Fair Chase</emph> magazine) was developed to inform Associate Members of
Club activities. </p>
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, candidate proposals,
membership lists, and drafts and planning materials related to the Associates
Newsletter. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, advertising, publicity
and promotional materials and materials related to assignments of copyright. Of
particular interest are assignments of copyright dating back to 1904.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This subseries contains correspondence, memoranda, and inquires
related to Club films and miscellaneous materials. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>In 1985 the Club formed the Boone and Crockett Club Foundation to
manage and direct the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch. The Ranch was
purchased by the Club to conduct research and educational activities related to
big game and conservation. In 2009, all physical assets, including the Theodore
Roosevelt Memorial Ranch, were transferred from the Foundation to the Club.
</p>
<p>This series contains correspondence, the Foundation’s Board of
Directors meeting minutes and by-laws, Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch
materials, financial and fundraising documents, and materials related to the
University of Montana Applied Research Program and Professorship. </p>
<p>Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no
discernable original order to the files. Materials were grouped and interfiled
by the processor to reflect historic organization of the Club’s Foundation.
Series are arranged alphabetically and original order within folders was
maintained. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This subseries contains annual meeting materials,
correspondence, meeting minutes, and by-laws.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This Subseries contains correspondence arranged in alphabetical
order. Of particular interest are folders containing the correspondence from
Club member Sherman Gray as these folders demonstrate and document the
development of the Foundation. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>Purchased in 1985, the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch was
purchased to conduct habitat and wildlife research and educational programs.
The Ranch was formerly managed by the Boone and Crockett Club Foundation. In
2009, the Ranch, along with all other physical assets, was transferred to the
Boone and Crockett Club. </p>
<p>This Subseries contains case statements, correspondence,
donation data, member mailers, research reports, and materials created by the
Ranch Management Committee. </p>
</scopecontent>

Professorship was established at the university. </p>

Montana, correspondence, reports, and miscellaneous materials. </p>

<p>The first folder contains correspondence from October 2, 1947 through
September 10,1948, much of which was generated by S.R. Logan in his capacity as
secretary of the Lake County Telephone Reorganization Committee, a few letters
by Ray Sprague, chairman of the same group, and responses from individuals,
government agencies, and businesses. The second folder contains items dated
from January1946 to February 1948 that include legal documents, research on
telephone associations, minutes of meetings, and expense records. The third
folder contains polling or survey forms, used in March 1948 to determine the
level of support on specific questions such as whether or not greatly expanded
telephone service was needed and if telephone lines should be installed on
power poles. The survey forms were sent to individuals, groups, and
businesses.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains genealogical information on many branches
from Fra Broadwell's family and Edwin Dana's family. There is correspondence
from family members to Fra and Edwin about their families histories. Some of
the families that have excellent research included are lines from the Anderson,
Brewster, Broadwell, Dana, Forester, Maxwell, Page, Paine, Putnam, and
Sunderland families, although this does not include all of the lines researched
in this collection. There are copied accounts from family members early
history, and publications on the Paine and Dana family.</p>
<p>Fra Dana also had publications on Astrology and scientific papers.
There are also notes on the Crow language from Father Prando and Fra's own
notes. Included also is a brand book of the cattle herd of the Blackfoot, which
was purchased by E.L. Dana.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes all of the genealogical information Fra Dana
was able to gather on family descent. There are twenty-six families researched
in this collection. Included is a direct line decent of Fra Broadwell Dana.
There are several marriage certificates. These include the certificate for the
marriage of John Sunderland to Elizabeth Page on February 14, 1819, a
certificate for Samuel F. Maxwell and Eliza Ann Sunderland on November 8, 1848,
a certificate for John W. Broadwell and Jewel H. Maxwell's marriage on May 12,
1873, and the marriage of E.L. Dana to Fra Broadwell on July 1, 1896. Parts of
a will for E.L. Dana dated to 1916 are included and a copy of the will for Ann
E. Broadwell dated to May 14, 1889, copied November 18, 1912 are included.
There are also applications to the Daughters of the American Revolution for
Jessie A. Sunderland (1899) and Emma R. Griffin (1909). The Paine and Dana
lines also have published material on their families.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes copies of accounts from early family history
from various family members, such as H.W. Baldwin (1895-1897), M.A. Whipple
(undated, 1935), Abraham Given (1850) and Theophilus and Debora Dana (1862).
Poems written by E.L. Dana (published 1947) and Edna Dinwiddie (copy undated)
are also included. There are copies of letters (undated, 1914, 1917-1918) from
World War I and papers (1915, 1917, 1926) from World War I--correspondents are
not identified by last name. There is a certificate from the Daughters of the
American Revolution (D.A.R.) and Colonial Dames of America (undated,
1911-1912). Jewel Dinwiddie's Daughters of the American Revolution pin and
tartan are in this collection as well. Family newspaper clippings are also
included. This series also includes notes on the Crow language from Father
Prando and Fra Dana and the brand book for the Blackfoot herd of cattle
(undated).</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This collection contains materials generated by Harry Fritz's time in the Montana Legislature
as both a state representative and a state senator. This includes constituent
correspondence, legislative information, notes, clippings, reports, news releases,
campaign materials, legislative journals, and election materials from the 1980s and
1990s. The collection also includes office files from Fritz's forty year career with
the Department of History at the University of Montana including lecture materials,
research notes, articles, speaking engagement notes, calendars, Montana centennial
materials, and manuscript reviews. The collection also includes several VHS tapes of
presentations and events associated with the Montana State Legislature.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The collection includes a broad range of John Rankin's financial
records, 1888-1906; speeches and clippings of Jeannette Rankin from 1916-1941,
her 1940 congressional run, and a
<title>Report of International Congress of Women</title>, 1919; and
Wellington Rankin's 1946 campaign and two Montana Supreme Court cases, 1925 and
1941, in which he served, respectively, as attorney for the plaintiff and
attorney for the defendant.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes some financial records from Rankin's most
notable endeavors such as the Rankin Block, the Rankin House, and lumber mills
in Missoula. Those records pertain to day-to-day operating expenses and income.
Two larger ledgers give a broader overview of Rankin's financial matters.
Wherever possible the records have been arranged chronologically but gaps do
exist.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes the trail transcript for the 1925 Montana
Supreme Court personal injury case of plaintiff, Velma H. Riggs, vs. defendant,
Lew Webb. Wellington Rankin served as the attorney for plaintiff, Riggs. The
series also includes the 1946 Montana Supreme Court decision in the case of
A.E. Cramer vs. The Montana State Board of Food Distributors. Wellington Rankin
served as an attorney for the defendants. The records of Wellington Rankin's
1948 congressional run include a pamphlet stating his platform and a copy of a
speech by Senator Dan W. Maddox endorsing Rankin's candidacy.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes a speech made by Jeannette Rankin on women's
suffrage, excerpts from other Rankin speeches regarding
<title>Measures Touching the Interest of the People of
Montana</title>, a radio address on
<title>Women and Democracy</title> by Rankin, and other speeches
discussing defense issues. The series also includes additional miscellaneous
material relating to Jeannette Rankin's 1940 congressional run.
<title>The Report of the International Congress of Women</title>,
which took place in Zurich in 1919, lists Jeannette Rankin as a delegate from
the United States. This volume has sections in English, French, and German.</p>

<p>The collection consists of the personal records of Harry W. Child and
the records of the Wylie Permanent Camping Company, Green Meadows Farm, the
Yellowstone Park Association, Yellowstone Park Transportation Company,
Yellowstone Park Company, Yellowstone Park Hotel Company, and Yellowstone Park
Camping Company. It provides documentation of park visitors, employees,
services, and the financial health of these companies.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains Harry W. Child's personal account books.
These contain financial records for his numerous real estate holdings in Helena
and Toston, Montana; Gallatin Gateway, Montana; Gallatin and Madison Counties,
Montana; and La Jolla, California. Many of the Helena records concern
construction of a root cellar. Many records deal with Yellowstone Park
ventures, including Yellowstone Park Transportation Company and Green Meadow
Farm. There are extensive records of the activities of Child &amp; Anceny,
which dealt in real estate and cattle ranching in Montana. The volume of deeds
and agreements concerns property transfers, many with the Northern Pacific
Railroad. There is extensive correspondence with his Bozeman attorney, Hartman
&amp; Hartman.</p>
</scopecontent>

Camping Company, which consists of records of supplies purchased. </p>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains a voucher register for the Yellowstone Park
Association, with record of supplies purchased. </p>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains the records of the Yellowstone Park
Transportation Company, which provided first railroad and stagecoach service in
the park, then automobile transport and services for visitors' automobiles.
Filling station and garage records are for Mammoth, Old Faithful, Thumb, Lake,
Fishing Bridge, and Canyon stations and show sales and the names of the
operators. There is also a list of supplies and services available at these
garages. The ledgers, journals, and voucher registers show operating expenses
for the YPTC. </p>
<p>The last portion of the series consists of records of Park
visitors from 1929 to 1951. The 1929-1930 book records visitors who entered the
Park at West Yellowstone, Gardiner, and Gallatin Gateway by rail and lists them
by state, town, and foreign country. The entrance registers, which run from
1946 to 1951, record visitors who entered the Park at Cody, Wyoming; Gardiner,
Montana; Mammoth; Red Lodge, Montana; Gallatin Gateway, Montana; Victor,
Wyoming; and West Yellowstone. Visitor information includes names, addresses,
and fees paid for transportation or car rental.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains records of the Yellowstone Park Company that
do not fall under the purview of one of the subsidiary companies. It contains
an employee register, fishing and boating records, a print shop inventory, and
general ledgers. The employee registers list all YPC employees for the 1934 and
1935 seasons, their position, and whether they arrived by rail or automobile.
There are both handwritten and typed versions of these records. Fishing and
boating records show boat rentals and other types of sale at the docks at Lake,
Fishing Bridge, Bridge Bay, and West Thumb. The general ledgers document
purchases of supplies, construction materials, and telegraph and railway
services, and document various other businesses operated in the Park.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains records of the Yellowstone Park Hotel
Company, which provided lodging services to Park visitors. The series consists
of financial records that record the details of the Company's financial health.
There is also a 1931 employee pay book from Mammoth, which lists employees by
name and occupation.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains the financial records of the Yellowstone Park
Camping Company, which provided campgrounds to Park visitors.</p>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection includes financial and legal records detailing the
daily operations of a small-scale western Montana lumber mill, with
particularly detailed records between 1944 and 1957. Most of the records are
handwritten journals or logs recording aspects of mill operations such as log
scale measurements submitted to the Montana State Forester for timber sale
review, payroll hours and rates, and daily product and administrative
transactions. Also included are typed records of quarterly production reports,
timber sale agreements, and union relationships. The union contract records
include correspondence regarding initial union representation for Morin Lumber
Company employees.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes a general equipment inventory, bound log
scale books, small bound payroll logs, unbound production reports, small bound
transaction journals, an unbound yard ledger, and five large bound ledgers of
outgoing lumber sales. All records are handwritten except production reports,
timber sale contracts, and union contracts. All bound transaction journals
exhibit accounting shorthand practices. Log scale books record timber
measurements submitted to the Montana State Forester as part of the timber sale
review process. Payroll records detail compensation by individual per pay
period, including per diem totals. Production reports detail lumber production
totals, equipment purchases, outgoing shipments, existing stock arranged by
tree species, and production lost to injury. General Accounts Journals record
daily transactions, credits, debts, and deposits. The yard ledger is an
alphabetized record of account activities from the Miller Creek mill operation.
Cash Books record sales of lumber leaving the processing yard.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes records detailing timber sale agreements and
union relationships. All timber contract records detail locations, total board
feet, and compensation. Most contracts in this collection were between Morin
Lumber Company and the State of Montana. Union contracts materials primarily
record personnel allocation agreements but also include official correspondence
between employees, union representatives, and mill ownership regarding the
initiation of union representation. All records are typed and in good
condition.</p>
</scopecontent>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The collection contains financial records including volumes for price
lists, engraver's records, outside and Butte shipping slips from 1926 to
1966.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series contains volumes of price list records, engraver's
records, outside shipping slips (for items shipped outside Butte), and Butte
shipping slips (for items shipped within Butte). The price lists detail the
description of the headstone, including the dimensions and the price that was
charged to the buyer. The volumes also include the name of the purchaser, the
date that the stone was processed and the time spent working on it. The volumes
are arranged alphabetically by the company's sizing system. The series also
contains the engraver's records which correspond to the records kept in the
price list volumes.</p>
<p>The volumes are organized by the job number of the stone. Outside
shipping slips are organized by the city in which the completed stone was sent,
such as Anaconda, Deer Lodge, Dillon, Helena, Idaho, and other outside states.
The records are organized by work number and include the name of the deceased
with the birth and death dates, the purchaser of the stone, and the date when
the order was paid in full. The shipper's name and address and shipment date,
and a detailed description of the stone are also in the outside shipping slips.
The Butte shipping slips contain the same information on them as in the outside
shipping slips except the name of the cemetery is included. The volumes are
arranged by name of cemetery, including Holy Cross, Mountain View, Mountain
Moriah, St. Patrick, and UG Weeks.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>James H. Morley's daily dairy accounts from 1862-1865 begin with his
trip to Montana from St. Louis, Missouri, onboard a steamer up the Missouri
River. It continues with his group's two week journey from Fort Benton to their
camp and mining site on Gold Creek, between what is now Drummond and Deer
Lodge, Montana, with supply loaded wagons. From that point his diary entries
describe the day's shaft or sluice mining efforts, reports from group members
who had traveled to other possible mining sites, and descriptions of his own
travels around Hellgate Canyon and into Rock Creek, then on to Beaverhead,
Flint Creek, Wisdom River, the Big Hole prairie, and back up to Deer Lodge
Creek. By January 1863 Morley and his team had ranged as far east in Montana as
the Gallatin and Three Forks areas. Also in January Morley noted the results of
a trial of Plummer, probably the infamous Harry Plummer, one year before that
man was hung by vigilantes without a trial. Morley briefly describes his own
contact with justice as a juror in a trial of accused murderer Bill Mitchell.
</p>
<p>Over the next two years Morley sometimes described the daily drudgery
of mining work but also mining claim disputes, planning and charting a plat map
for Centreville, wildlife and geological features, scouting for and staking new
claims, difficulties of sending and receiving mail, and the mining towns of
Bannack and Virginia City, Montana. His daily entries end with his return to
St. Louis in August, 1865.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection includes a photocopy of Helen Edna Buck's thirty-two
page, handwritten letter to Clara Ballard (addressed as Dear Friend) detailing her family's move from Yakima, Washington to
Rhodes, Iowa. Buck describes the weather, roads, camp sites and camping
conditions, livestock and wildlife encounters, interesting geology, towns and
people they encountered. The towns in Montana included Saltese, St. Regis, Huson, Missoula, Butte, Whitehall, Custer, Miles City, Glendive, and Wibaux. Their route included the road called the Camel's Hump. She also writes of going through Yellowstone Park, car
trouble, and how she felt about her new home. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>John Well-Off-Man's Collection of Photographs contains 109 images of people and events on the Rocky Boy's Indian Reservation. The photographs were taken during the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries. Well-Off-Man collected these images from Paul Mitchell, an elder from Rocky Boy's Indian Reservation, as part of his research into the history of the Rocky Boy Reservation. Well-Off-Man made copy negatives from Mitchell's nitrate negatives.</p>
<p>A portion of the images in this collection have brief descriptions written on them, though it is not clear by whom. Almost all the images are undated and many currently lack identification of the individuals in them. Most are of Cree and Ojibwe (Chippewa) people. While the images in the collection come from several sources, the majority were likely taken by John Gable, the son of William Gable who was the Lutheran Pastor on the Rocky Boy Reservation in the 1920s, 30s, and 40s. As a graduate student at the Philadelphia Seminary in the 1930s, John Gable was also responsible for a number of film productions including "Rocky Boy Mission In Action," a 1935 film about the Lutheran Mission on the Rocky Boy Reservation. While it is unclear whether the photos in this collection are associated with Gable's documentary project, the content of the images suggest that there is a connection between the two. According to Well-Off-Man other images were taken by Florence Bruckner.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains materials related to the development,
operation and dismantling of the Douglas Mine and Concentrator, located in
Granite County, Montana, by the Montana Phosphate Products Company and Cominco
American, Inc. during the 1960s and early 1970s. The records offers insight
into mining philosophies and trends of that time, as well as providing
information on the day-to-day operations of a phosphate mine and milling
operation in Western Montana. </p>
<p>Series I, Mine and Concentrator Development, contains materials
related to the development of the Douglas Operation by the Montana Phosphate
Products Company, and later Cominco American, Inc., beginning in 1962 and
extending into mid-1960s. Included are cost quotations and advertisements for
various mining and milling equipment, engineering drawings, construction
specifications, cost projections and other materials. This series gives an
overview of state-of-the-art phosphate mining technologies in the 1960s, as
well as the amount of financial investment and work necessary to undertake such
a mining project. </p>
<p>Series II, Mine and Concentrator Operations, contains daily and
monthly reports, maintenance schedules, studies, correspondence, financial
calculations, and other miscellaneous materials created by the Montana
Phosphate Products Company and Cominco Amerincan, Inc. during the operation of
the Douglas Mine and Concentrator from 1962-1968. This material provides a look
into the day-to-day operations of a phosphate mine and concentrator operating
in Western Montana during the 1960s. </p>
<p>Series III, Concentrator Dismantling, contains correspondence and
daily reports, as well as other miscellaneous material related to the
dismantling of the Douglas Concentrator in 1972. This action was authorized by
Cominco American, Inc. and carried out by the Bechtel Corporation. The series
is representative of how Cominco American, Inc. was able to salvage much of the
equipment at its Douglas Creek location for use in another mining project in
Greenland. </p>
<p>Series IV, Maps and Drawings, contains numerous oversized maps and
drawings depicting the Douglas Operation and other Montana Phosphate Products
Company and Cominco American, Inc. mines in the region, including the Anderson
(Warm Springs), Brock, Luke, and Relyea Mines. The materials range in subject
from underground mines to dam cross-sections to construction specifications.
</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>The Peggy DeMichele papers contain photos, speeches, and documents of Montana Congressman James O’Connor, with whom DeMichele worked prior to Mike Mansfield, as well as her personal ephemera and photos. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains letters from customers throughout Montana and
nearby states ordering fruit from Theon H. Durnford in Lolo, Montana,
1913-1924, with the bulk from 1918, and Durnford's receipts and statements from
Hughes Mercantile of Lolo, Montana, from 1917-1919.The bulk of the letters are
orders for Theon H. Dunford’s fruit but a few letters also contain personal,
cultural, and social information on topics including the influenza epidemic,
the scarcity of workers during the First World War, and oil drilling. The
letters also offer information about the varieties of fruit Durnford grew, how
these fruits were shipped, how customers chose to use the products, and how a
small agricultural business functioned at the time. Durnford shipped his fruit
both to individual customers and retail distributors. Many of his customers
were in Big Timber, Three Forks, Toston, and Townsend, Montana.</p>
<p>The receipts and invoices from Hughes Mercantile record Durnford's
sale of eggs to the store in exchange for everything from laundry to canned
peas and chicken feed.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>Receipts and statements for items bought and sold at Hughes
Mercantile in Lolo, Montana. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The John M.Clifton photograph album contains photos of timber work out
of St. Regis, Montana in 1909; the construction and camp sites for building the
Big Blackfoot railway branch in Montana in 1910; the Colgate, North Dakota
railway branch from 1910-1911; and the Wenatchee, Washington railway branch
from 1912-1913. The album also contains a few family photos of John M. Clifton,
his wife Nora Toole Clifton, and their baby daughter, Thula Clifton.</p>

<p>This collection contains materials related to the research and writing
of Oberdorfer’s book,
<title>Senator Mansfield: The Extraordinary Life of a Great American
Statesman and Diplomat </title>(Smithsonian Books, 2003), which won the D.B. Hardeman Prize in 2003.
The book is a biography of Mike Mansfield, a United States House Representative and Senator
from Montana who also served as ambassador to Japan during the Carter and
Reagan administrations. The collection provides access to the documents and
other materials that Oberdorfer cites in his book,
<title>Senator Mansfield</title>. The research materials include
photocopies and summaries from books and articles about Mansfield and related
historical topics, as well as primary documents gathered from archival
repositories like the presidential libraries of John F. Kennedy and Lyndon B.
Johnson. The research materials provide glimpses into Mansfield’s personal life
and public career through copies of correspondence, photographs, and other
materials from the private collections of Mansfield family members. </p>
<p>The collection includes summaries of Oberdorfer’s conversations with
Mansfield’s family, colleagues, and friends and some drafts of chapters from
Oberdorfer’s book. Manuscript drafts and writings related to the book are filed
with the research materials. The collection also contains recorded interviews with Mansfield
and Mansfield's colleagues that Oberdorfer conducted as research for the Mansfield biography,
as well as non-interview audio recordings related to Oberdorfer's research.
</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent><p>The collection includes summaries of Oberdorfer’s conversations with Mansfield’s family,
colleagues, and friends and some drafts of chapters from Oberdorfer’s book. Manuscript drafts and writings
related to the book are filed with the research materials. </p></scopecontent>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The collection contains a variety of materials collected and produced
by Haugland as part of his journalism career, personal writing, and enduring
interest in the military. Correspondence from his career was mostly conducted
for research purposes and includes exchanges with many military personnel.
Writings include manuscripts of articles, including those written for the
Associated Press and his novel. There are financial materials related to his
many travels for his work, along with his travel documents like passports.
There are research materials related to NASA and the space program, as well as
K'tut Tantri in Indonesia. There are clippings of many of his articles, some
personal materials, and memorabilia. Last, there are photographs of Haugland
and that he collected for his work.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series contains correspondence that Haugland conducted with
various people throughout his career with the Associated Press and into his
retirement. Haugland conducted correspondence with his research subjects,
including the Eagles, an American World War II flying force fighting for
Britain before America entered the war, and K'tut Tantri, and Indonesian women
who Haugland made the subject for one of his manuscripts. Haugland also
corresponded with Great Britain's Prince Philip in his research of the Eagles,
who made him an honorary member of their group. Haugland had a great deal of
correspondence with book companies who wanted Haugland to write for them. He
also corresponded with military personnel, many of whom were personal friends
of Haugland's because of his NASA splashdown coverage for the AP.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series is divided into two subseries: Manuscripts and
Datelines. The first portion is manuscripts of articles and his novel
manuscripts. The second part of the series is Haugland's datelines that he
wrote for the AP. Many articles that Haugland wrote dealt with the avionics
industry, including airplanes, military bombers and the NASA space exploration.
He also wrote many articles and two books on the experience of the Eagles
during WWII. Copies of his manuscripts of
<title>Eagle Squadron</title> and
<title>The Eagle's War</title> are in the series. Many of his
research notes are also included. Another book manuscript,
<title>Revolt in Paradise</title>, is in the series. The datelines
are mainly written about the avionics industry. Many news stories are about
NASA and the different space missions, including the Apollo and Gemini flights.
Other news stories on which Haugland reported were events in the Soviet Union,
Vietnam, Japan, and the South Pacific.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series contains general and travel receipts from the many
locations in which Haugland traveled to for the Associated Press. Also in the
series are his expense accounts and tax information, including tax returns. The
series is arranged in two parts. The first part, general financial records, is
arranged chronologically.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series consists mainly of documents from Haugland's years as a
war correspondent. They include his license, passports, war correspondent
agreement contract, orders, a permit to leave the United States, and an
Australian registration. Other documents in the series are agreements with
publishing companies for Haugland's manuscripts, such as Harper and Brothers
and Spartan Books.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>The series contains materials that Haugland used in research for
his articles. The majority of research materials are about NASA and the space
program. Haugland covered the Apollo missions, Gemini and Voyager. Other topics
that Haugland researched were the places he traveled, military, and K'tut
Tantri in Indonesia. He also collected numerous materials on the Eagle
squadrons, the American pilots who flew for the British during WWII.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series of articles is divided into two subseries: Vern
Haugland and Other Authors. Most of the clippings by Haugland are written on
the NASA space program, and center on the Apollo missions, missile testing, and
army rocket tests. People that Haugland wrote about were Charles Lindbergh,
General Douglas MacArthur, and Admiral Richard Byrd. Other topics that he was
interested dealt with aviation, including air travel, airports, and different
types of aircrafts. The articles written by other authors that Haugland
collected dealt with the NASA space program, missile testing, and satellites.
Other topics included moon research, the Eagle Squadron, and the Air Force.
Articles written about the Haugland family and Haugland himself are also in the
series. Many of these articles are about Haugland's time in New Guinea and the
book that Haugland wrote about his experiences, his war years, and copies of
his obituaries after his death in 1984.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series consists of booklets and pamphlets from many of
Haugland's memberships, including the Aviation Writers Association and the
National Aeronautic Association. His work journals are also included in the
series, and many are written in shorthand. Haugland kept travel receipts and
memorabilia from the Pacific island and Soviet Union trips that he took while
working for the Associated Press. He received many certificates and citations,
such as honorary memberships from the many ships that he traveled on while
covering the NASA splashdowns and awards from writing associations.
Correspondence with his wife, Tess, and his daughters is also in the series.
There is also biographical information on Haugland in the series. A WWII based
novel is also included within the series. This book deals with the war's 100
most fascinating stories. Haugland's story about his ordeal in New Guinea is
included in the book.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series contains artifacts that Haugland collected during his
years with the Associated Press. Many of the artifacts relate to aviation, such
as a wing remnant from the New Orleans first round-the-world flight in 1924 and
a plaque commemorating the first flight by the Wright brothers in 1903. Other
memorabilia centers on the NASA space program, mainly the Apollo missions. Also
in the series are artifacts dedicated to Haugland on the numerous awards that
he received. He received the Associated Press Medal of Honor, the Associated
Press Strebig-Dobben Memorial Award, the Air Force Association Arts and Letter
Award. Haugland also received an airplane propeller in 1973 signed by his
friends in aviation.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series consists of photographs of Haugland and his career,
and of photographs he collected in the course of his work. The latter mostly
relate to the military and aviation.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This series includes twelve aircraft lithographs presented to
Haugland as a gift from Northrop Aircraft Inc. at an unknown date.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent>
<p>This photocopied collection is composed of a newspaper clipping dated
July 15, 1865, Franklin Miller's diary from January 1-August 5, 1867, and his
1866 identification card at Fort Riley, Kansas.</p>
<p>The newspaper clipping is from a
<title>Soldier's Letter, Second Colorado Calvary</title> of Fort Riley,
Kansas. It describes Indian attacks, battles, deaths, and other news, military
and general.</p>
<p> Franklin Miller's diary begins January 1, 1867, and contains accounts
of the weather, the regiment, deaths of men in the company, burials,
correspondence with family and friends, company inspections, deserting
soldiers, arrival of recruits, and Miller's discharge from Camp Cooke on August
5, 1867. The diary also records the passing of several steamer ships and
contains two poems written by Franklin Miller.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains correspondence, financial, legal,
promotional, and organizational records generated by the Collins Land Company
as well as government publications regarding federal public lands and business
records from three other Collins family enterprises. The Collins Land Company
was based in Helena, Montana, and bought and sold public lands. Materials in
this collection provide particular insights into the history, procedures, and
economy of public land management and sale during the first half of the
twentieth century.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains incoming, outgoing, interoffice and general
correspondence generated and collected by the Collins Land Company detailing
business projects, proposals, and practices spanning the first four decades of
company operation. Series materials are almost exclusively exchanges with
clients, potential buyers, and Federal land management officials. These records
provide insights into the procedures and economy of public land sales during
the first half of the 20th Century.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains land scrip case histories collected by the
Collins Land Company as documentation for title purchases and transfers. The
Collins Land Company created four distinct sequences for these case histories
and attached a case number to each file (beginning at zero for each sequence).
The original sequences and case numbers have been retained for historical
reference; however, records explaining the tracking system rationale and
detailing gaps in each sequence no longer existed at the time the collection
was accessioned to the archives. These records provide early property
definitions and ownership histories for land parcels across the United States,
with particular emphasis on Montana and the Pacific Northwest.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains one folder of financial records, 10 bound
financial volumes, and one folder of legal documents generated by the Collins
Land Company, including two volumes tracking account activity for land scrips
allotted to Union Civil War veterans and soldiers who fought in the
Spanish-American War. Legal documents include property deeds, prospecting
patents, and court transcripts.</p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="5202_">
<p>This series contains Collins Land Company publications and
advertisements as well as an extensive sequence of Federal government
publications relating to management and dissolution of public lands. These
government publications include Congressional legislation and U.S. Department
of the Interior regulations.</p>

<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>This collection contains the personal and professional papers of Dr.
Jessie Bierman, a pioneer in the field of child and maternal health, from all
stages of her life. The collection contents begin with writings related to
Bierman’s family history. The collection contains the memoirs of Jessie
Bierman’s father, Henry, and her writings about him. </p>
<p>Items from her early days include a poetry scrapbook filled with
correspondence and poems, her high school yearbooks, and diploma. Her student
days at The University of Montana are represented by a scrapbook and diploma.
Materials from her medical career in California include a set of house call
diaries, 1931-1935. A scrapbook and related correspondence represent her years
with the Montana Department of Health. Her positions in government and with
international missions related to maternal and child health are reflected in
correspondence and other writings. The collection contains the writings and
publications Bierman completed while at the University of California and
elsewhere, including the study she prepared regarding the children of Kauai,
Hawaii. </p>
<p>The collection contains the numerous honors and awards Bierman
received toward the end of her career. It also contains clippings about Bierman
and other clippings and publications she collected on child and maternal health
issues. The photographs in the collection are from all stages of Bierman’s
life. Of particular interest are the family photographs, which include
photographs of the Kalispell Meat Market that was owned and operated by Henry
Bierman, and photographs of Henry and Alice Bierman. </p>
</scopecontent>
<scopecontent encodinganalog="520">
<p>The collection includes the 119-page manuscript of Violet Dunbar's
unpublished book, Homesteaders in Montana.</p>
